  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e404bfd5-5aaf-4533-b210-61d86d5ce091'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489905722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3926250588167229843"><blockquote>"<i><b>Remember that hope is a good thing, Red, maybe the best of things, and no good thing ever dies.</b></i>"</blockquote><i>Rita Hayworth and The Shawshank Redemption</i> is subtitled 'Hope Springs Eternal' - and that perfectly sums up the soul of his book. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402692i/782877._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It's hope that keeps you going - even after everything horrible that you can ever imagine has already happened to you, even after life has knocked you down over and over again, even after there seems to be nothing left. <b>Hope is the last thing to die, they say.</b> Andy Dufresn</span>
  <span id="freeText3926250588167229843" style="display:none"><blockquote>"<i><b>Remember that hope is a good thing, Red, maybe the best of things, and no good thing ever dies.</b></i>"</blockquote><i>Rita Hayworth and The Shawshank Redemption</i> is subtitled 'Hope Springs Eternal' - and that perfectly sums up the soul of his book. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402692i/782877._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's hope that keeps you going - even after everything horrible that you can ever imagine has already happened to you, even after life has knocked you down over and over again, even after there seems to be nothing left. <b>Hope is the last thing to die, they say.</b> Andy Dufresne has taken that saying to heart, apparently.<br><br><i>The Shawshank Redemption</i> is a prime example of why Stephen King will always remain among my favorite authors. Branded a horror writer, a representative of a genre that is so easy and tempting to altogether judge and dismiss by book <s>snobs</s> lovers¹ <i>(and I have been among them on more than one occasion, I must confess)</i> results in way too frequent overlooking of his captivating storytelling skills and excellent character development that is the driving force behind his stories. His best books - and this is one of them, undeniably - are based on <i>"what if?"</i> approach, and then watching his characters try to find their way out of the <i>"what if?"</i> situation, shaping themselves in the process of writing into fully fleshed figures which are so much more than just the vehicles for necessities of plot development.<blockquote>¹ From <a href="http://journal.neilgaiman.com/2012/04/popular-writers-stephen-king-interview.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman's interview with King</a>:<br><br><i>"I was down here in the supermarket, and this old woman comes around the corner, this old woman – obviously one of the kind of women who says whatever is on her brain. She said, </i>'I know who you are, you are the horror writer. I don’t read anything that you do, but I respect your right to do it. I just like things more genuine, like that Shawshank Redemption.'<i><br>And I said, </i>'I wrote that'.<i> And she said, </i>'No you didn’t'<i>. And she walked off and went on her way."</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402692i/782878._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Shawshank Redemption</i> is the story narrated by Red, a prisoner at the fictional Shawshank prison in Maine, immortalized by Morgan Freeman (what a fitting last name!) in a well-known Frank Darabont screen adaptation of this book. Red tells us the story of his fellow prisoner Andy Dufresne, falsely accused of a murder he did not commit and sentenced to a life behind bars as a result. Andy, a small calm level-headed former banker, who would seem to be destined for the role of perpetual victim in the place where brawn seems to be worth more than brains, where he has met violence and humiliation and senseless brutality from both guards and prisoners. <b>It was a place destined to break Andy's spirit. It's supposed to do that to everyone.</b> That's the point.<br><br><b>And yet Andy Dufresne calmly refuses to be broken.</b> Andy so fiercely clings to his humanity, to his hope that he becomes a legend. His demeanor - that of a free man even caged seemingly forever - is what gives hope to others, especially Red, his friend and narrator.<blockquote>
  <i>"So yeah - if you asked me to give you a flat-out answer to the question of whether I'm trying to tell you about a man or a legend that got made up around the man, like a pearl around a little piece of grit - I'd have to say that the answer lies somewhere in between. All I know for sure is that Andy Dufresne wasn't much like me or anyone else I ever knew since I came inside. He brought in five hundred dollars jammed up his back porch, but somehow that graymeat son a bitch managed to bring in something else as well. A sense of his own worth, maybe, or a feeling that he would be the winner in the end... or maybe it was only a sense of freedom, even inside these goddamned gray walls. It was a kind of light he carried around with him."</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402692i/782879._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Andy Dufresne meticulously and patiently clings to a bit of hope, so irrational and fickle that anyone would have given up. And it's this hope, so inherent to his nature, that allows him to retain his humanity and quiet but undeniable dignity in a place where neither is supposed to exist. Violence, corruption, power, greed, cruelty - Andy goes through it all with his unexpected backbone of steel, allowing all of it to only barely tarnish his amazing resilient spirit, winning his little victories against the system along the way, in his own way brightening the existence of those for whom there'd appear to be little left, patiently fighting his fight to keep little glimpses of humanity in the place where they are rarely seen.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402692i/782880._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>"Some birds are not meant to be caged, that's all. Their feathers are too bright, their songs too sweet and wild. So you let them go, or when you open the cage to feed them they somehow fly out past you. And the part of you that knows it was wrong to imprison them in the first place rejoices, but still, the place where you live is that much more drab and empty for their departure."</i>
</blockquote>I first read this book as a fourteen-year-old teenage cynical know-it-all - and when I got to the end, I cried. Because it hit me then how, despite my teenage sense of invulnerability, the world can be cruel to you for no reason, and sometimes hope is all you have left. Now I'm twice that age, having seen a bit of the life's cruelty that King so frequently alludes to, and I no longer cry at the ending of this book; instead, I marvel with a feeling of sadness and quiet fascination at how aptly he captured the need to keep going despite all odds, even when it appears there is nothing left to live and hope for. <b>Because hope dies last, and sometimes you just need to see it through to the end. And as long as you haven't lost yourself, your inner little sense of worth, there remains something to live and fight for.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402692i/782881._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>"I find I am excited, so excited I can hardly hold the pencil in my trembling hand. I think it is the excitement that only a free man can feel, a free man starting a long journey whose conclusion is uncertain.<br>I hope Andy is down there.<br>I hope I can make it across the border.<br>I hope to see my friend and shake his hand.<br>I hope the Pacific is as blue as it has been in my dreams.<br>I hope."</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3926250588167229843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5329422576890669299"><b><u>Prison ain't no fairy tales.</u> </b><br/><br/>Almost everything that could be possibly said about it has been said. What makes this book different is the message it conveys - one of eternal hope. I was and am profoundly moved by this simple and eloquent depiction of hope, friendship, and redemption. <br/><br/>The story begins with the trial of a young banker, Andy Dufresne, victimized by circumstantial evidence, resulting in a conviction for the murder of his wife and her lover. After a quick conviction, Andy finds himsel</span>
  <span id="freeText5329422576890669299" style="display:none"><b><u>Prison ain't no fairy tales.</u> </b><br /><br />Almost everything that could be possibly said about it has been said. What makes this book different is the message it conveys - one of eternal hope. I was and am profoundly moved by this simple and eloquent depiction of hope, friendship, and redemption. <br /><br />The story begins with the trial of a young banker, Andy Dufresne, victimized by circumstantial evidence, resulting in a conviction for the murder of his wife and her lover. After a quick conviction, Andy finds himself serving a life sentence at Shawshank prison, with no hope of parole.<br /><br />Stephen King is one of the most enchanting storytellers of our time, and perhaps, the only one alive. His prose is equally enchanting, wonderful, and mesmerizing. It was a sheer delight to read him. And, by the way, it was my first Stephen King novel. All in all this is a great story vividly told that will leave you with a true sense of redemption in your soul. It is a riveting tale about friendship and the strength of character, about going up against what is wrong and unfair and coming out on top through pure true grit and a little luck, that will leave you in utter amazement! <br /><br /><b>It is such a moving tale that you just can't help but love it.</b><br /><br /><br />Highest Recommendations!</span>

<div id="review_2192554329" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2192554329" />
    <a title="Mort" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67602782-mort"><img alt="Mort" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586932919p2/67602782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2192554329?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mort" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mort" href="/user/show/67602782-mort">Mort</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2192554329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer839982535818703563">This is going to be a different kind of review.<br/>While we all know that the book is better than the movie - no, this is not a debatable statement...while I strongly feel that everybody is entitled to their opinion, you are wrong if you don't agree and it's time somebody is brutally honest with you - we tend to forget that adapting a book into a screenplay is a writing art of its own.<br/><br/>The writer of the screenplay will always be at a disadvantage when adapting a book, especially when it is a popular </span>
  <span id="freeText839982535818703563" style="display:none">This is going to be a different kind of review.<br />While we all know that the book is better than the movie - no, this is not a debatable statement...while I strongly feel that everybody is entitled to their opinion, you are wrong if you don't agree and it's time somebody is brutally honest with you - we tend to forget that adapting a book into a screenplay is a writing art of its own.<br /><br />The writer of the screenplay will always be at a disadvantage when adapting a book, especially when it is a popular story already. Here are some of the disadvantages:<br />* Time - In the movie industry, one page roughly translates to one minute on screen. This means that most producers of movies, unless it is a well established writer to begin with, will not even consider a script of more than 120 pages, and they prefer 90 - 100 pages. To condense any book down that much usually means some things has to be sacrificed, already taking away some of the magic of the story.<br />* Control - Once a screenplay is sold to a movie studio, in most cases, all control of the story and the written word is given up. The director can chop and change anything to make the vision he/she has of the movie into a reality. Sometimes it is practical reasons - the budget doesn't allow it, the correct location couldn't be found, the weather is not working along, etc. - and sometimes it's just a silly expression of art, but the story can be...ahem, excuse the crudeness..."whored down" for whatever reason. And, to top it all off, the powers that be can decide that the ending needs to be more "viewer friendly" and insist on a change - <i> Great respect to Brad Pitt who threatened to withdraw from the movie SE7EN if they changed the ending, and therefor ensuring one of the best movies ever was released! </i>.<br />* Ego - Ah, yes, the thing that makes Hollywood go round...I think a lot of people will be shocked if they found out how many times lines had to be changed to make it "funnier" or to make the best-paid actor look better on screen. How horrific...<br /><br />Right, so the reason I chose this book to write the review on is because I have great respect for the man who adapted this brilliant Stephen King novella for the screen - Frank Darabont.<br />This is, in my opinion, one of the best adaptations out there. Darabont was also the director of the movie, which helped with the control. And throw Morgan Freeman in the cast, you know it has to be, at the very least, a good movie.<br /><br />This was also the first "dollar-deal" - and I haven't researched this, only read about it many years ago, so correct me if I'm wrong. Stephen King made a deal with some aspiring screenplay writers that he would sell the rights to some of his stories to be adapted into screenplays for a dollar. Don't misunderstand, it's a dollar and they had the right to adapt the screenplays, not the rights to the entire story. I'm pretty sure he made a decent amount of money from the movies.<br />Anyway, Darabont adopted this story into THE SHAWSHANK REDEMPTION and it impressed King enough to allow him to try and sell it. And the rest is history - this is a brilliant story (thank you Mr. King) told brilliantly on screen (thank you Mr. Darabont).<br /><br />Darabont would make two further "dollar-deals" with King, maybe you've heard of them:<br />THE MIST will be the lesser known of the two. I absolutely LLLLOOOOOVVVVEEEEDDDD the end of that movie.<br />THE GREEN MILE...need I say more.<br /><br />Darabont will also be the one who will bring THE WALKING DEAD to the small screen - and I'm going to leave it at that because they fired him during the second season and everything went to shit from there.<br /><br />What's the best adaptation you've seen?</span>
  <a data-text-id="839982535818703563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2519511722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2519511722" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2519511722?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2519511722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9176532199147588767"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467148388ra/19558490.gif' width='400' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I've watched <i>The Shawshank Redemption</i> movie any number of times on cable TV (at least the last half of it; I almost always manage to miss the first half). So a few weeks ago when my husband asked me to find Stephen King's story <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11574.The_Body' title='The Body by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Body</a> (the basis for the movie <i>Stand by Me</i>), I was delighted to find the novella <i>Rita Hayworth and the Shawshank Redemption</i> in the same collection. My husband hasn't read his story yet, but I've read mine. :)<br/><br/>A lifetime convict, Red (in the story, a redheaded man of Iri</span>
  <span id="freeText9176532199147588767" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467148388ra/19558490.gif" width="400" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've watched <i>The Shawshank Redemption</i> movie any number of times on cable TV (at least the last half of it; I almost always manage to miss the first half). So a few weeks ago when my husband asked me to find Stephen King's story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11574.The_Body" title="The Body by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Body</a> (the basis for the movie <i>Stand by Me</i>), I was delighted to find the novella <i>Rita Hayworth and the Shawshank Redemption</i> in the same collection. My husband hasn't read his story yet, but I've read mine. :)<br><br>A lifetime convict, Red (in the story, a redheaded man of Irish descent :( - no Morgan Freeman) narrates the story of Andy Dufresne, his unjust imprisonment for murder in Shawshank Prison, and his life and times in prison. Andy is a standoffish guy, but Red is the guy who can get almost anything for you (he draws the line at weapons and hard drugs). Gradually the two become friends. Red watches as Andy deals with the prison rapists called the sisters, and then becomes valuable to the prison guards and the warden himself because of his financial wizardry. Despite his circumstances, Andy has hope and a self-confidence that Red admires. <br><br>It was so interesting to see where the movie follows the original story and where it diverges. I like some of the changes introduced in the movie, actually, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[especially Andy's final fleecing of Warden Norton and the warden's final fate <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But the theme of personal redemption came through for me more strongly in this story.<blockquote>Remember that hope is a good thing, Red, maybe the best of things, and no good thing ever dies.</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1536174607ra/26257399.gif" width="317" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Content notes: disturbing discussion of prison rape and prison life, a couple of uses of the N word to describe how prisoners are treated, an F-bomb or two.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9176532199147588767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1430499618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1430499618" />
    <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor"><img alt="Fabian {Councillor}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599133151p2/40792319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430499618?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian {Councillor}" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor">Fabian {Councillor}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430499618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3880831270252988466">Usually, I'm struggling with trying to review my favorite books, because apart from expressions like 'awesome', 'mind-blowing' or 'must-read', not too much can be said about stories like these. Perhaps this is one of the reasons why I tend to enjoy writing snarky reviews of books I disliked way more than trying to compose a decent review on a story I loved and want everyone else to read as well.<br/><br/>"Rita Hayworth and Shawshank Redemption" is one of them. I have to admit, I am a huge fan of prison st</span>
  <span id="freeText3880831270252988466" style="display:none">Usually, I'm struggling with trying to review my favorite books, because apart from expressions like 'awesome', 'mind-blowing' or 'must-read', not too much can be said about stories like these. Perhaps this is one of the reasons why I tend to enjoy writing snarky reviews of books I disliked way more than trying to compose a decent review on a story I loved and want everyone else to read as well.<br /><br />"Rita Hayworth and Shawshank Redemption" is one of them. I have to admit, I am a huge fan of prison stories and the way they are able to explore what imprisonment and isolation from society can do to a human's mind. Stephen King managed to explore this in such a perfect way, allowing hope and despair to flow into his words simultaneously. I've read many other reviews emphasizing it, and I can only sign what they are writing: this is not only a story about life in prison (which, by the way, is depicted in a very realistic way - not that I would be able to judge how life in prison really feels like, but at least King managed to convince me this is how it <i>would</i> feel like to be imprisoned for more than thirty years), but also a story about hope. And it is perfectly done. Not many stories before have been able to nearly reduce me to tears at the ending, but "Shawshank Redemption" is one of them.<br /><br />It's no long story and, thus, will not take much time to read, so I can highly recommend giving it a try. Now, watching the movie version with Morgan Freeman and Tim Robbins will gain a high place on my to-do-list (right beneath reading more Stephen King novels), as nearly everybody seems to have watched this movie - and loved it - except for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3880831270252988466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1271498934?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelli" href="/user/show/4146551-kelli">Kelli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4146551-kelli?shelf=audio">audio</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1271498934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2152601924509899294">Anyone driving north on Rte 3 "down in Massachusetts" this morning may have passed a girl driving an SUV, one hand covering her mouth, tears pouring down her face and neck. They may have wondered in passing if she was having a rough morning or had received some bad news...but would anyone ever guess that she was in throes of this cathartic sobfest courtesy of Stephen King and the beautiful final passages of The Shawshank Redemption? Probably not.<br/><br/>I cannot believe I have never read this. Actually,</span>
  <span id="freeText2152601924509899294" style="display:none">Anyone driving north on Rte 3 "down in Massachusetts" this morning may have passed a girl driving an SUV, one hand covering her mouth, tears pouring down her face and neck. They may have wondered in passing if she was having a rough morning or had received some bad news...but would anyone ever guess that she was in throes of this cathartic sobfest courtesy of Stephen King and the beautiful final passages of The Shawshank Redemption? Probably not.<br /><br />I cannot believe I have never read this. Actually, I listened to the audio and the narrator was superb. Having seen the movie countless times and identifying it as my all-time favorite, I pictured Morgan Freeman and Tim Robbins throughout the story but that neither added to nor detracted from the experience for me...and this was just that...an experience. I am at a loss to articulate how truly magnificent this story is. The cadence and vernacular were perfection and the story was nothing short of brilliant: a story about friendship, hope and perseverance that will have you smiling through tears at the end. 5 stars.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624580279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9875047280011865535">Full Video Review Here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/2hPmd3LCklU'>https://youtu.be/2hPmd3LCklU</a><br/><br/>It's really amazing to think that a story that has become so embedded into our pop culture and so many people still have no idea it's a Stephen King story. In 1982, he proved that he was more than just the "scare the pants off of you" author, but he could also write something uplifting and emotionally powerful as the best in the game.<br/><br/>This is THE story of resiliency, never giving up hope. Putting your faith in something that should be out of you</span>
  <span id="freeText9875047280011865535" style="display:none">Full Video Review Here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/2hPmd3LCklU">https://youtu.be/2hPmd3LCklU</a><br /><br />It's really amazing to think that a story that has become so embedded into our pop culture and so many people still have no idea it's a Stephen King story. In 1982, he proved that he was more than just the "scare the pants off of you" author, but he could also write something uplifting and emotionally powerful as the best in the game.<br /><br />This is THE story of resiliency, never giving up hope. Putting your faith in something that should be out of your control but finding a way to overcome against all odds. But it's also a story of true friendship between two men from completely different worlds.<br /><br />It is absolutely amazing what King was able to do with just 100 pages in this story. It never once feels rushed yet flies through decades of times spent within the walls of Shawshank. If I have a single gripe about this story it would only be that I wish it was a full-length novel.<br /><br />If you love the movie, and chances are that you do, do yourself a favor and pick up the novella. There's a reason it's one of the best Stephen King adaptations; because it's one of the most faithful.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4812426422299244647">Absolute brilliant novella about two long term prison inmate in Shawshank. You'll learn a lot about prison routine and how Red and Andy Dufresne came along. Why is Andy, a banker inside. Did he really murder his wife and her golf teacher? What about Rita Hayworth? Did she really visit that prison or is there another connection to her? Stephen Kind does an absolute outstanding job here. One of the best prison stories ever written. At the end there is quite a surprising twist. The characters menti</span>
  <span id="freeText4812426422299244647" style="display:none">Absolute brilliant novella about two long term prison inmate in Shawshank. You'll learn a lot about prison routine and how Red and Andy Dufresne came along. Why is Andy, a banker inside. Did he really murder his wife and her golf teacher? What about Rita Hayworth? Did she really visit that prison or is there another connection to her? Stephen Kind does an absolute outstanding job here. One of the best prison stories ever written. At the end there is quite a surprising twist. The characters mentioned are extremely well done. The prose exceptional (it's Red's story). Real life or life behind bars, there are many parallels. We also learn that hope is the most important thing. Awesome novella, absolutely recommended!</span>

<div id="review_3742925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3742925" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/183285-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184807670p2/183285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3742925?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/183285-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Horror fans, Stephen King fans, book-to-film buffs</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/183285-mark?shelf=kingstephen">kingstephen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3742925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11743052322149254827">One of the best set of novella length stories ever put together. Period. For anyone out there who accuses King of not beinjg able to write well, this set should end that argument.<br/><br/>Shawshank: "Rita Hayworth and the Shawshank Redemption" is a masterpiece. A streamlined cast of characters and clever telling of the story using the narrator as a main character, only to shift into first person to finish the story with expectant yet unresolved hope.<br/><br/>Apt Pupil: Scary. Really spooky stuff. Not so much for </span>
  <span id="freeText11743052322149254827" style="display:none">One of the best set of novella length stories ever put together. Period. For anyone out there who accuses King of not beinjg able to write well, this set should end that argument.<br /><br />Shawshank: "Rita Hayworth and the Shawshank Redemption" is a masterpiece. A streamlined cast of characters and clever telling of the story using the narrator as a main character, only to shift into first person to finish the story with expectant yet unresolved hope.<br /><br />Apt Pupil: Scary. Really spooky stuff. Not so much for the blood and gore, although I had an itchy feeling know how much thought the author put into how to properly knife a hobo to death. No, the creepiest idea is that a person could come so far off the tracks and still be able to function undetected in society. Very believably done.<br /><br />The Body: Almost sweet in its recollection of waning childhood. A story of friendships doomed to end, innocence dead but not yet buried, and a quest to see something awful leads to understanding. Written by another man at another time, this story might be considered a classic. I hope someday it's recognized as such.<br /><br />Breathing Method: The weakest sotry of the bunch, and tip of the hat to people who love King for his ability to shock and get all the "gooshy" stuff just right. Simple put, the story itself isn't up to par with the other three. Still a must read for King fans, but the odd man out in this set.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11743052322149254827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

You can't read/talk about this book without referencing its movie counterpart, because after all, Shawshank Redemption is one of the most popular and well-liked movies of all time. Another reason is that the book and movie are almost exactly alike. Sure, there are a few bits in the book that the movie leaves out, and a modicum of poetic justice is doled out in the movie that doesn't happen in the book. Otherwise though, they're one and the same, and I love them both!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15532937589769660793"><i>
  <b>“Some birds are not meant to be caged, that's all. Their feathers are too bright, their songs too sweet and wild.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>For me, The Shawshank Redemption is one of the best, most memorable films ever made. I will assume that every one here has watched it or at least knows the story, so I won't talk about the plot. I knew I was going to love the story even before I began reading it because of my love for the film.<br/><br/>I wonder why King didn’t write this story as a full novel but it doesn’t need to be lon</span>
  <span id="freeText15532937589769660793" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Some birds are not meant to be caged, that's all. Their feathers are too bright, their songs too sweet and wild.”</b>
</i><br /><br />For me, The Shawshank Redemption is one of the best, most memorable films ever made. I will assume that every one here has watched it or at least knows the story, so I won't talk about the plot. I knew I was going to love the story even before I began reading it because of my love for the film.<br /><br />I wonder why King didn’t write this story as a full novel but it doesn’t need to be long to be powerful. Isn't it? The language and characters are so raw and real I found it hard to switch back to reality after reading this story. The character development in this story is remarkable.<br /><br />It’s a stunning story about corruption, friendship and hope. How King provokes emotion in the story is remarkable. The ending was one of the best “feel-good” endings I've ever read.</span>

<div id="review_3621752657" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3621752657" />
    <a title="Stacy Fetters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29942945-stacy-fetters"><img alt="Stacy Fetters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573594587p2/29942945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3621752657?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacy Fetters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacy Fetters" href="/user/show/29942945-stacy-fetters">Stacy Fetters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781982155759" href="/book/show/52730699-rita-hayworth-and-shawshank-redemption">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3621752657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5727998685428291027"><b>“Remember that hope is a good thing, Red, maybe the best of things, and no good thing ever dies.”</b><br/><br/>I broke my own rules with this book. I've seen the movie before I read the book. Okay, here's the deal. The movie came out in 1994 and I wasn't even ten years old yet. But why my parents let me see this film? I'll never know. <br/><br/>Shawshank Redemption is one of my favorite movies and when they re-released this short story in paperback, I knew that I needed this edition for my collection. We all know how t</span>
  <span id="freeText5727998685428291027" style="display:none"><b>“Remember that hope is a good thing, Red, maybe the best of things, and no good thing ever dies.”</b><br /><br />I broke my own rules with this book. I've seen the movie before I read the book. Okay, here's the deal. The movie came out in 1994 and I wasn't even ten years old yet. But why my parents let me see this film? I'll never know. <br /><br />Shawshank Redemption is one of my favorite movies and when they re-released this short story in paperback, I knew that I needed this edition for my collection. We all know how the story goes but I was interested in reading this for two reasons: Stephen King is a master storyteller making him one of my favorite authors and I wanted to see how much the book differs from the movie. And I am proud to announce that not much was different. A few things were off but I believe that was to beef up the movie a bit and make it more exciting. <br /><br />Stephen King knows how to capture an audience with his captivating way of bringing a story to light. His mesmerizing words are crafted flawlessly as the story progresses. You can't help but be dazzled by his stories filled with dread and sometimes redemption. This one was just as fantastic as his other novels and paired with a great film, it makes this pair unstoppable. I can't recommend this book enough!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5727998685428291027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_946402522" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/946402522" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/946402522?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781101010990" href="/book/show/9836767-the-shawshank-redemption">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer946402522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18322004267613748850">This is such a wonderful story. It's the "Hope Springs Eternal" portion of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39662.Different_Seasons' title='Different Seasons by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Different Seasons</a>. That sounds ridiculous on the surface because, it is after all, about a man wrongfully convicted of a double homicide and then incarcerated for decades, but somehow King infuses each page with hope. Even the pages that talk about lining your underwear with toilet paper because you've been raped! Any writer that can do that is a magician and a genius in my opinion!</span>
  <span id="freeText18322004267613748850" style="display:none">This is such a wonderful story. It's the "Hope Springs Eternal" portion of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39662.Different_Seasons" title="Different Seasons by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Different Seasons</a>. That sounds ridiculous on the surface because, it is after all, about a man wrongfully convicted of a double homicide and then incarcerated for decades, but somehow King infuses each page with hope. Even the pages that talk about lining your underwear with toilet paper because you've been raped! Any writer that can do that is a magician and a genius in my opinion!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18322004267613748850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2514694062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2514694062" />
    <a title="Eliza Rapsodia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6561375-eliza-rapsodia"><img alt="Eliza Rapsodia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597687917p2/6561375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2514694062?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eliza Rapsodia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eliza Rapsodia" href="/user/show/6561375-eliza-rapsodia">Eliza Rapsodia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Todo el mundo</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Eliza by: </span>
      nadie
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6561375-eliza-rapsodia?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6561375-eliza-rapsodia?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6561375-eliza-rapsodia?shelf=need-to-buy">need-to-buy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2514694062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6703580761397842937"><b>REVIEW IN ENGLISH</b><br/><br/>As it happens sometimes, <b> I had not read the original material behind one of my favorite movies of all time. </b> And I was really surprised when I found out that behind a wonderful movie <b> is a short story by Stephen King. </b> An author who can also write stories without supernatural aspects that can leave you breathless. And this is one of them.<br/><br/>Andy Dufresne is a banker who is accused of murdering his wife and her lover.<b> He is finally sentenced to two life sentences. </b> When he is sent </span>
  <span id="freeText6703580761397842937" style="display:none"><b>REVIEW IN ENGLISH</b><br><br>As it happens sometimes, <b> I had not read the original material behind one of my favorite movies of all time. </b> And I was really surprised when I found out that behind a wonderful movie <b> is a short story by Stephen King. </b> An author who can also write stories without supernatural aspects that can leave you breathless. And this is one of them.<br><br>Andy Dufresne is a banker who is accused of murdering his wife and her lover.<b> He is finally sentenced to two life sentences. </b> When he is sent to Shawshank Prison in 1948, he does not talk much but he has an unnatural tranquility. Ellis Boyd Reddind called "Red" is a red-haired convict who can get what you need —from posters, gum, cigarettes or drugs—. Over time, Red and Andy become good friends and Andy tell him that he is innocent of the crime he is accused. <b> It is Red who tell the story of his friend's hope and redemption.</b><br><br><img height="214" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536423628i/26273208.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Tim Robbins and Morgan Freeman as Andy and Red<br><br>The Shawshank Redemption is a 1994 film starring Tim Robbins and Morgan Freeman. It went unnoticed in the Oscars that year, also because it had hard competition (Pulp Fiction and Forrest Gump),so didn't win any award. <b> But over the years many voices rose up saying how wonderful it was and the position it truly deserved among the best films of the decade and of all time. </b> While the movie change things and add scenes (Red is red-haired not black for example), they are good decisions because they add to the story.<b> So you can imagine what the short story is like.</b><br><br>From Red's perspective, <b> we will know not only why he got in prison, also the decades locked in with Andy Dufresne, </b> who suffers the worst humiliations imaginable but continues to stand firm and not succumb to sadness and despair. Over time, Andy becomes an important person in Shawshank as his talent and knowledge with numbers is and taxes is known. He manages to work in the prison library and improve the lives of his inmates friends, but he will be very persistent to do so.<br><br>Andy liked to play chess, carve figures with stones and minerals and hanging posters of female movie stars on his cell, <b> being Rita Hayworth the first one he asked Red to get for him.</b> Over the years, Andy and Red and their friends become inseparable. <b> But Red notices that Andy is different, he seems to be made of another material, one unbreakable.</b><br><br>King made the characters alive and well fleshed out. With less than 180 pages we get to know the decades in the fictional jail of Maine and the political and corruption aspects behind the condemnation of innocent people. <b>This story is not only about prison life and how life changes us and we get used to being locked up and we no longer know how to live, but how good things never die and one of them is hope, something that can keep a person alive and not let it fall despite all the bad that can happen. </b><br><br>Certainly worth reading. This story was also published in Different Seasons, a short story collection. Highly recommended. One of the best of the year.<br><br><b>*********************************************<br><br>RESEÑA EN ESPAÑOL</b><br><br>Como pasa a veces <b>no había leído el material original detrás de una de mis películas favoritas de todos los tiempos.</b> Y supongo que me llevé una gran sorpresa cuando me enteré que detrás de una maravillosa película 
  <b>e</b>
<b>stá una historia corta de Stephen King, </b>un autor que puede dedicarse también a escribir historias sin tintes sobrenaturales que te pueden dejar maravillado. Y esta es una de ellas.<br><br>Andy Dufresne es un banquero que es acusado de asesinar a su esposa y al amante de ésta. <b>Al final es condenado a dos cadenas perpetuas. </b>Cuando lo envían a la prisión de Shawshank en 1948  no suele hablar con nadie pero tiene un aura de tranquilidad. Ellis Boyd Redding o Red para los amigos es un convicto pelirrojo que puede conseguirte lo que necesites desde afiches, chicles, cigarrillos o drogas. Con el tiempo, Red y Andy se vuelven buenos amigos y Andy le confiesa que es inocente de lo que se le acusa. <b>
  Es Red quien contará la historia de esperanza y redención de su amigo.
</b><br><br><img height="214" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536423628i/26273208.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Tim Robbins y Morgan Freeman como Andy y Red<br><br>The Shawshank Redemption en inglés es una película de 1994 protagonizada por Tim Robbins y Morgan Freeman. Pasó desapercibida en los Oscars de ese año por tener una dura competencia (Pulp Fiction y Forrest Gump ni más ni menos) y no se llevó ningún premio. 
  <b>Pero con los años muchas voces se alzaron diciendo lo maravillosa que era y el puesto que merecía entre las mejores películas de la década y de todos los tiempos. </b>
Si bien la cinta agrega cambios y escenas (Red es pelirrojo por ejemplo), no molestan en absoluto porque están bien hechos y agregan más de lo que quitan. <b>
  Entonces ya se pueden imaginar como es la historia corta. 
</b><br><br>Desde la perspectiva de Red <b>
  vamos a conocer no solo porqué él llegó a prisión sino como fueron las décadas encerrado con Andy Dufresne,
   
</b>quien sufre los peores vejámenes que se puedan imaginar pero siempre trata de mantenerse firme y no sucumbir a la tristeza y la desesperación y con el tiempo se convierte en una pieza importante en la cárcel, <b>ya que se hace conocido su talento y conocimiento para las cuentas y los impuestos. Con esto logra encargarse de la biblioteca y logra mejorar la vida de sus compañeros, pero siendo muy persistente.</b><br><br><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jVrWv_evv1A/W5KUn0cNDNI/AAAAAAAANQM/R9IeryTHQbkFCcIlFREchl1rzN0yhpGwwCLcBGAs/s1600/Sue_o_de_fuga-379877672-large.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="225" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536423628i/26273209.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Andy le gustaba jugar al ajedrez, tallar figuras con piedras y minerales y le gustaban los afiches de las estrellas de cine del momento, <b>
  siendo Rita Hayworth la primera elegida que le pide a Red que le consiga. 
</b>Con los años los lazos entre el grupo de amigos se va cerrando y Andy y Red llegan a ser inseparables.<b> Pero Red nota que Andy es diferente, parece estar hecho de otro material, uno que parece inquebrantable.</b><br><br>La narración de King hace que los personajes cobren vida y se hagan tridimensionales, se hace cercano y en poco más de ciento cincuenta páginas logremos conocer las décadas en la cárcel ficcional de Maine y los aspectos políticos y de corrupción detrás de la condena de personas inocentes. Esta historia no es solo sobre la vida carcelaria y cómo la vida nos cambia y nos acostumbramos a estar encerrados y ya no sabemos como ser de otra manera,<b> sino como las cosas buenas nunca mueren y entre esas está la esperanza, </b>algo que puede mantener la fe intacta de una persona y no dejarla caer a pesar de todo lo malo alrededor. <br><br>Sin duda vale mucho la pena leer esta historia. En español se publicó en la colección de historias llamada Las cuatro estaciones. <b>
  Altamente recomendada. De lo mejor del año, sin duda.
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6703580761397842937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17344299611651273341">I hadn't read a truly frightening book of his. Yes, King's novels are disturbing, but not scary. A truly powerful yet disturbing account of an injustice law system, and the effects it has on a young man's life. Although imprisoned unjustly, he doesn't complain: it is not in his character. Instead, he decides to fight the system: not with his fists, with his mind. He succeeds. If you liked the movie, you will not be dissapointed in the moody, honest and bold novel. But in the sad case when you ha</span>
  <span id="freeText17344299611651273341" style="display:none">I hadn't read a truly frightening book of his. Yes, King's novels are disturbing, but not scary. A truly powerful yet disturbing account of an injustice law system, and the effects it has on a young man's life. Although imprisoned unjustly, he doesn't complain: it is not in his character. Instead, he decides to fight the system: not with his fists, with his mind. He succeeds. If you liked the movie, you will not be dissapointed in the moody, honest and bold novel. But in the sad case when you haven't seen the movie, don't read the book.</span>

<div id="review_56482144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56482144" />
    <a title="April" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1405910-april"><img alt="April" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574686846p2/1405910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56482144?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April" href="/user/show/1405910-april">April</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio Cassette 9780140862133" href="/book/show/531681.The_Shawshank_Redemption">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1405910-april?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1405910-april?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1405910-april?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56482144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12380177349792681607">I am willing to bet the majority of people reading this review have already seen the film version of The Shawshank Redemption. If you have not seen the movie, stop reading my review and go watch the film. It is amazing. I have recently discovered the 'free' audio-books on the library. (Thank you tax dollars). The Shawshank Redemption by Stephen King is a relatively short book. It is also a short audio book, only 3 cassettes (my POS car has a tape-deck). Frank Muller narrates Stephen King's tale </span>
  <span id="freeText12380177349792681607" style="display:none">I am willing to bet the majority of people reading this review have already seen the film version of The Shawshank Redemption. If you have not seen the movie, stop reading my review and go watch the film. It is amazing. I have recently discovered the 'free' audio-books on the library. (Thank you tax dollars). The Shawshank Redemption by Stephen King is a relatively short book. It is also a short audio book, only 3 cassettes (my POS car has a tape-deck). Frank Muller narrates Stephen King's tale of prison life. Here's the thing, if you must audio a cassette, don't get an old cassette from the library, buy a new one. With me, it just skipped and pretty much stopped playing, so I had to plead with the powers that be to let me finish the story of Red and Andy Dufresne.<br /><br />Bitching and moaning aside, I thought Frank Muller's voice was perfect for the story. He sounds like a grizzled felon with a heart of gold. As audio-book connoisseurs know, the voice really adds or detracts from a book.<br /><br />I felt the characters were fascinating. I genuinely liked Andy Dufresne, disliked the corrupt guards known as screws, and Red - the man who can get you anything in prison. Andy embodies hope within the most confining circumstances, jailed for murder of his wife and her lover -- he really has little hope of parole. There's no way he'd ever get out, as the DA used Andy's case as leverage into a higher position. You have the guards who represent the institution, who do their best to exploit Andy's tax-preparing expertise, and try to squelch Andy's hope. You have Red who's been in jail for so long that it feels safe to him, he has a position of prominence within the prison as the man who can get anything. Red makes for an intriguing study of the psychological effect of institutionalization.<br /><br />I loved King's writing style, he can really make me guffaw, then feel broken hearted, then fit to burst with joy all on one page. I know some people hate King and his super-long books, but I am an unabashed King fan. I think there is a reason he is the king of horror, and I think his efforts to reach into other genres are fantastic (i.e. The Green Mile -- wasn't horror to me), so maybe I do have some bias. I love that King makes me contemplate the freedom of being able to see the night-sky unimpeded by bars.<br /><br />However, I will admit, I felt the movie was definitely better. There is a reason it is the number one user voted film on IMDB.com.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12380177349792681607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17657524846125511510">I can't believe it took me this long to discover this novella, especially since The Shawshank Redemption is my all time favorite movie. Hearing the story from Red's gentle and detailed perspective was intriguing. Red has a great sense of humor throughout the book. He tells the story in a way that allows you to see the passing of time. This is not as evident in the movie version. Although short, this book gives the reader something to hope for in their own life. I also loved the peek into the pri</span>
  <span id="freeText17657524846125511510" style="display:none">I can't believe it took me this long to discover this novella, especially since The Shawshank Redemption is my all time favorite movie. Hearing the story from Red's gentle and detailed perspective was intriguing. Red has a great sense of humor throughout the book. He tells the story in a way that allows you to see the passing of time. This is not as evident in the movie version. Although short, this book gives the reader something to hope for in their own life. I also loved the peek into the prison world. It's hard to imagine the living conditions that some prisoners face. Best of all I think was that Red was a murderer. That may seem irrelevant. However, I feel that Red did change. He made a mistake, but that mistake was not the entirety of his existence. He was a man with deep emotion, skill, trustworthiness, and he was Andy's friend. This bond between two strangers is one of my favorite tales ever told. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17657524846125511510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2008423575" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2008423575" />
    <a title="Mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23106940-mia"><img alt="Mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600049623p2/23106940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2008423575?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mia" href="/user/show/23106940-mia">Mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=best-villains-ever">best-villains-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2008423575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8120576030488028491">"<i>Well you weren't writing about yourself,</i> I hear someone in the peanut-gallery saying. <i>You were writing about Andy Dufresne. You're nothing but a minor character in your own story.</i> But you know, that's just not so. It's <i>all</i> about me, every damned word of it. Andy was the part of me they could never lock up, the part of me that will rejoice when the gates finally open for me and I walk out in my cheap suit with my twenty dollars of mad-money in my pocket. That part of me will rejoice no matter ho</span>
  <span id="freeText8120576030488028491" style="display:none">"<i>Well you weren't writing about yourself,</i> I hear someone in the peanut-gallery saying. <i>You were writing about Andy Dufresne. You're nothing but a minor character in your own story.</i> But you know, that's just not so. It's <i>all</i> about me, every damned word of it. Andy was the part of me they could never lock up, the part of me that will rejoice when the gates finally open for me and I walk out in my cheap suit with my twenty dollars of mad-money in my pocket. That part of me will rejoice no matter how old and broken and scared the rest of me is."<br /><br />God, I love this story. It really is timeless, and just wonderful. It's a story in the old fashion, with an incredible plot and characters that interact meaningfully and a great setting that binds it all up... There's nothing abstract or unreachable about it, and I think it's one of the most accessible and easy-to-relate-to tales I've ever read. There's just something about <i>Rita Hayworth and Shawshank Redemption</i> that plays into our human desires: the desire for justice, the burning need we have for wrongs to be put right, the way we respect and root for people who deserve better than what they got. It's so appealing on so many levels, and since it's well-written and touching to boot, this story really is perfect.<br /><br />I've mentioned elsewhere how I love moral greyness and the vast area between black and white, but every now and then I need some good old-fashioned good vs. bad, wrong vs. right. I've loved books with almost no plot to speak of—<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6288.The_Road" title="The Road by Cormac McCarthy" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Road</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20575425.Wolf_in_White_Van" title="Wolf in White Van by John Darnielle" rel="nofollow noopener"> Wolf in White Van</a>—but now and again I need a simple yet compelling plot, one that makes sense and has all the trapping of a story. Not a character study, not an exploration of morality, a STORY. Sometimes as a reader I feel like a child who just wants to curl up and listen to their parents read them a bedtime story, and while Red makes it clear that prison is no place for fairytales, this one has that same calming, spellbinding effect.<br /><br />The film adaptation of this is my favourite movie of all time, as I suspect is the case for many people, and I know you're wondering: Which is better, the movie or the book? Well, I'll have to chalk this one up to one of those rare occasions like The Princess Bride where they're both equally great. I have to give credit to the filmmakers here, because they kept all the good parts intact and left everything more or less unchanged, and what they added enhances the story rather than obscures it. I'm also kind of in awe as to how they captured Red's voice so well; even apart from the voice-over parts (most of which is exact quotes from the novella), the way the plot unfolds is so spot-on when compared to the narrator's straightforward, earnest, yet thoughtful way of storytelling in the novella.<br /><br />Other than that, there's not too much more I can say, other than I recommend this novella to... well, pretty much everyone. If you have a heart and a pair of eyes and the ability to read, you'll find something to love about this story.<br /><br />_______________________________<br /><br /><br />PRE-REVIEW, 25 AUGUST 2017:<br /><br />Here I am sitting in a hair salon among the sounds of ladies chattering and blowdryers and pop music, blinking away tears, feeling like the oldest ex-con walking away from Shawshank Prison, getting his first taste of that cold bracing air that whispers <i>freedom</i>.<br /><br />Hope springs eternal, indeed.<br /><br /><br /><br />Review to come shortly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8120576030488028491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EpOd4legnYRU22nqzjweWzoO4dTJWILdHXlk3TQ/dAReR98rWVVI4SAib2kpQd8RSYi50RZYte5cSBzW6d29jA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+VeWNZDzmQVyGcPZ5sOFSeaZYrUnTmBwMqzH6vTkioi1g9T8ngZMYAbgxVoBvkQDlR86sPhOV0Nznb/hKQZDAA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
750,358
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6322258409747007024">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText6322258409747007024" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6322258409747007024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
